Top

19-band surface reflectance (Curtin U) - MODIS

The Moderate Resolution Imaging Spectroradiometer (MODIS) was designed to meet the needs of the science community for frequent, high quality observations of global atmospheric, oceanic and ecological systems metrics and information. Much effort has been directed at validation and comparison of MODIS based ecological variables. Significant and complex issues remain in the use of the data over the Australian land surface, particularly over the Australian bright arid and semi-arid regional environments. These challenges include the accurate atmospheric correction of MODIS visible observations. Any limitations in the quality of atmospheric correction of MODIS data have implications for all products derived from visible observations. Recognizing this, TERN/AusCover developed an atmospheric correction algorithm for Australian MODIS land-surface observations that meets several specific needs:
- incorporates best available ancillary data sources
- can be applied to current and historical MODIS observations
- can be efficiently implemented on computing facilities available to AusCover
- and is easily extendible to provide VIIRS (or other instrument) atmospheric correction.

The Simple Method for Atmospheric Correction (SMAC) meets these requirements and forms the basis of the AusCover SMAC for MODIS (ASM).These data should be cited as made available by through TERN/AusCover and accessed on

Department of Environment and Natural Resources, Government of South Australia

The Department of Environment and Natural Resources (DENR) is South Australia's lead environment agency. We bring together conservation of the environment and the management of natural resources. Our responsibilities include natural resources management (NRM), nature conservation, heritage conservation, coast and marine conservation and animal welfare. We manage approximately one quarter of the state's land in the public land estate and manage important cultural institutions such as the botanic gardens.http://static.ecoinformatics.org.au/denr.jpg

Top

EVI - MODIS datacube MOD13Q1 spikes removed

EVI time series over some land cover types sometimes contain 'spikes' and sharp drops that do not represent biophysical changes on the earths surfaces. These spikes need to be removed prior to further analysis. This dataset uses an algorithm described in the technical report available at http://www.ga.gov.au/earth-observation/landcover.html. to remove spikes/sharp drops from the EVI dataset. The dataset has also been 'transposed' from individual EVI timeslices into a datacube that can be used for multiteporal analysis.
Monthly NDVI is a composite of the NDVI values from cloud-free observations in the month from the operational afternoon NOAA satellite. There are, in the absence of cloud, usually one and sometimes two observations per day. The satellite data are processed initially onto a 0.01x0.01 degree grid and then averaged to a 0.05x0.05 degree grid. The data is available within a few days after the end of a month.These data should be cited as made available by through TERN/AusCover and accessed on
Top

Biological Database of South Australia: Distribution and Habitat of Native mammals at Mt Billy

Mammal survey in 1998 of Mt Billy Park including native mammal list and their distribution within vegetation habitats. In particular looking at the distribution of bandicoots and pygmy possums and their habitation of fire-affected parts of the park. Biological Database of South Australia: Muraltia heisteria control at Morialta

Muraltia heisteria is a regionally significant weed that successfully invades quality bushland. This weed has been removed by hand over a number of years. Biological Database of South Australia: Sheoak Germination Trial (Coffin Bay NP)

Aim was to monitor Sheoak seedling survivorship in different areas within Coffin Bay National Park. Germination was not found to be a problem when growing Sheoaks. Biological Database of South Australia: Ngarkat Conservation Park Dingo Baiting Program

Since 1995, perimeter and internal baiting of the Ngarkat Conservation Park has been conducted at baiting stations located 10 km south of the northern boundary and at the Piggery at 15 km. 10 stations at each locality are marked with painted droppers 30 cm from the track and have baits placed each February, May, August and November. Records of bait uptakes have only been collected over the past 2 years.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Reedy Lagoon Revegetation and Hydrological Monitoring

Reedy Lagoon is held as a "Minister's Reserve" (Water Reserve No.3; near Penola ) under the Crown Lands Act. An adjoining landowner has an annual licence for sheep grazing only. Revegetation trials for woodland habitat have been undertaken. There are concerns that the regional groundwater table is dropping reducing the period of inundation of the swamp. Photopoints and piezometer monitoring is undertaken several times a year (1988-2001).Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem / Biological Database of South Australia: Fauna Population Study: Fairview Wetlands Monitoring

The Fairview Wetlands are 3 wetland basins situated on properties. These wetlands had varying salinities - marine to fresh - but the Fairview Drain decreased their periods of inundation. Pumps were installed in the Fairview Drain to artificially re-instate an appropriate wetting and drying system. Wetland habitat was fenced off and revegetation works undertaken. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Kaiser Stuhl Conservation Park Riparian Review (Working Group Proposal)

Following Yalumba's construction of major dams upstream of Kaiser Stuhl Conservation Park on Tanunda Creek in the early 1990's, concern was expressed over environmental issues of local riparian health and observed degradation resulting from changes in stream flow patterns. A working group recommended various actions involving monitoring of stream vegetation, water quality, sediment movement and aquatic biota. These separate monitoring actions, using a variety of monitoring methods are linked to other programs, all combined to provide an indication picture of the state of riparian ecosystems.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Fauna Population Study: Lower Glenelg River CP small mammal population monitoring

Small mammal population monitoring (2001-2011) initially Southern bandicoots but now swamp antechinus and nationally threatened mammals in reserve (Glenelg River), including heath mouse and long-nosed potoroos. Biological Database of South Australia: Fauna Population Study: Watervalley Wetlands Management Plan

Management Plan for several wetlands in the Watervalley Wetlands. Hard copy only of report exists (1992). Information includes hydrology, soils, vegetation associaitions, water control structures, commercial uses, and waterbird breeding and maintenance records, including indications of numbers of breeding sites. Biological Database of South Australia: General Purpose Photopoint: General Trends in Vegetation Recovery - Flinders Ranges

A number of permanent monitoring sites have been established on the Flinders Ranges National Park to enable long-term evaluation of vegetation responses to management programs aimed at reducing total grazing pressure. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Plant Species Structure in Ngarkat CP in Relation to Fire History

A series of 8 structurally similar vegetation sites in Eucalyptus sp. scrub of varying fire histories spanning from approximately 1945 to 1999 were sampled in the northern portion of Ngarkat Conservation Park to determine how plant diversity and structure is affected by time since burn. Biological Database of South Australia: Biological Survey of South Australia: Belair Recreation Park (NPWS 1981)

The Belair National Park was surveyed in 1978 to sample the vegetation of the range of vegetation associations systematically, using a series of grids and to map the major vegetation associations using aerial photography. The survey also sampled vertebrate fauna at a series of sites within each vegetation association in a systematic and repeatable manner.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Fauna Population Study: Fox Control Baiting - Belair NP, Scott Creek CP and Mark Oliphant CP

Assess the uptake of 1080 fox baits and the success of fox control in 5 Southern Lofty District parks including Cleland National Park, Belair National Park, Mark Oliphant Conservation Park, Scott Creek Conservation Park and Onkaparinga National Park (1992-2007). Originally conducted in conjunction with larger land care or Friends groups. Bait stations are laid with 1080 Foxoff baits during Autumn, carcases are accurately located and dated, bait offtake recorded and data sheets.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Roadside Vegetation Survey: Roadside Veg RVR3 - Mt. Pleasant LGA

Roadside vegetation survey for (part of) the Mt. Pleasant Council using standard drive-by roadside vegetation survey methodology. Data is used to determine Vegetation Associations along roadside vegetation corridors, their condition and conservation status. This data is then used by local councils to assist in managing their native vegetation. The surveys were carried out on many council managed roads within Mt. Pleasant Council area (580.95km) during 1997/1998.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Rare and Threatened Species Protection Strategies: Monitoring regent parrot nest colonies along the Murray River Corridor

The program is being conducted by the Friends Group. Data collection involves visiting areas likely to be utilised by Regent Parrots (Murraylands) and waiting until they return to the nest to rest, then recording the sites of the nests (GPS?). It is likely that site codes will be established for each nest to ensure each tree has a unique ID. The nests will then be monitered over time.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia

The Biological Database of South Australia (BDBSA) is the primary store for biodiversity information within the Department of Environment and Natural Resources of the Government of South Australia. The BDBSA manages specimen and observation records and includes taxonomic systems for South Australian flora and fauna. BDBSA data supports decision making on environmental issues within the South Australian and Australian governments as well as the wider community with an interest in biodiversity conservation.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Chowilla monitoring program exclosure data

Herbivore exclosures were set up on Chowilla Pastoral Lease in 1986 to determine the effects of grazing and grazing suppression on populations of Atriplex stipitata. The current project has 5 exclosures that vary in size from sets of 3 x 1/2 ha or 3 x 1 km which make large exclusion zones. Each exclosure was grazed previous to the survey and each has different objectives. The vegetation data is recorded and photos are taken for each. The monitoring is irregular in frequency.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: REptile Assemblages in the Mount Lofty Ranges - Postgraduate studies

The study was conducted in 25 fragments of native vegetation in the Southern Mt Lofty Ranges. It assessed the use of nested subset analysis as a conservation tool. This will allow establishment of gradient in proneness to extinction (predictable extinction sequence). This in turn allows to identify species sensitive to habitat fragmentation and therefore extinction. It would then be easier to prioritise conservation management actions. Furthermore, vested subset analysis can be used to suggest what factors might be contributing to the composition patterns within a community.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Recovery of Senecio megaglossus in Dutchman's Stern Conservation Park

Growth and recruitment of a population of Senecio megaglossus (rated as vulnerable under the EPBC Act, 1999) has been monitored to evaluate the impact of goat grazing on the long-term survival of the species in the southern Flinders Ranges (Dutchman's Stern Conservation Park). A goat proof grazing exclosure was constructed in 1993 and details of the layout are contained in a report by R Davies 1995 titled Threatened Plant Species in NP&W Act Reserves in South Australia. Surveys have been conducted at irregular intervals since 1992.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Malleefowl Release (Lincoln NP)

In 2002, four captive bred Malleefowl were released in Lincoln National Park. There is Radio Tracking data and Breeding Records: number of eggs hatched for the first year. Radio tracking discovered that one male had paired up with what is believed to be an existing female and an active mound was found in late 2002. DEH & EPNRM staff has been monitoring known mounds in the park during the breeding season and the mound was found to be active again in the 04/05 breeding season.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Adelaide & Mount Loft Regions (AMLR) Threatened Flora

Threatened Flora in the Adelaide & Mount Lofty Ranges. This aim of this project is to implement recovery actions identified from the AMLRRRP for threatened flora in the Adelaide & Mount Lofty Ranges region. This involves population surveys of priority threatened flora species. Surveys are coordinated by the DEH Threatened Flora Ecologist, Adelaide Region. Data collected includes species name, GPS coordinates and datum, date, location description, and population size.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: SE Native Fish Sites

Over 35 sites have been assessed by DEH in 2009 for the presence and abundance of native freshwater fish. This information will update the DEH SDE Native fishlayer for the south-east of SA . The update of the fish layer with south east data is specifically required for completion of the Lower South East Adaptive Management Scoping Study project.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Calperum

The aim is to monitor the effects of recovery from de stocking at Calperum. This was the initial site where the methods were established. No exclosures in this project. Vegetation monitoring and rangeland assessment. Photopoint project, photos taken annually and a soil and vegetation analysis is done quarterly. The Pastoral technique was adopted for the survey and it covers all three stations. Data is used to review past and work out what to do in the future in regards to grazing pressure. Point based information has been documented.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: SSAA Goat Control Programs - Bounceback (SthFlinders,Bimbowrie, GammonRangesNP)

Numbers of goats shot by members of the Hunting and Conservation Branch of the Sporting Shooters Association of Australia during regular ground - based goat culls on Flinders Ranges National Park and Vulkathunha - Gammon Ranges National Park. Also includes bimbowrie. Data includes sex and age class of goats shot. Gammon Ranges began in 1992 and Flinders Ranges in 1993. Ongoing monitoring. 3 programs per year at Vulkathunha - Gammon Ranges National Park. 1 program per year at Flinders Ranges National Park.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Conservation of Red Gums in the Flinders Ranges

A collection of photographic images showing the condition of river red gums throughout the Flinders Ranges. Sites range from Port Germein to the Gammon Ranges and many are taken in National Parks of the ranges. This collection possibly accompanied a report on condition of the red gums. The images illustrate various growth stages in various localities and also show the impacts of disturbances including water stress, cockatoos, insects and pathogens.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Winninowie CP Biological Survey

Project to undertake a survey of fauna and flora species with in the Winninowie Conservation Park. The aim of the project is to provide a better understanding of the species within the area for conservation purposes. The project was also used to improve the skill and training of regional staff in plant and animal identification, safe animal trapping practises and animal handling techniques. Trapping was conducted at 4 sites, over 4 nights (October 17-21 2008). Four vegetation sites (30m x 30m) also surveyed.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Mary Seymour Conservation Park Prescribed Burning Assessment

Mary Seymour Conservation Park has a small infestation of buckthorn, (Rhamnus alaternus) amongst Melaleuca brevifolia closed shrubland habitat. A small prescribed burn was undertaken in August 2001 to assess effectiveness of fire in removing buckthorn. Burn was undertaken on 14 August 2001 and follow-up photopoint and plant count (tea-tree and buckthorn) monitoring. Monitoring program to culminate in report to NVC ~ May 2002 - depending on results may undertake larger burn for whole population.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Ngarkat CP Fire History Maps (1945 - 2002)

Aerial photography of the Ngarkat Conservation Park Complex and neighbouring Heritage Agreements has been used to map fire histories covering the period 1945 - 2002. A3 sized maps have been retained within District offices that can be overlaid to compare vegetation responses and extent of burns. Various thematic maps can be produced using ArcView software to incorporate other spatial layers onto the fire frequency layer that provide a long term vegetation monitoring tool for park management.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Arcoona Creek Vegetation Exclosures

The effects of rabbits and feral goats on the growth and regeneration of perennial vegetation at Arcoona Creek are studied in a series of fenced vegetation exclosures and associated unfenced plots. Rabbit, goat and kangaroo (euro) densities are estimated from annual dung collections. The location and height of selected perennials are recorded annually, on maps of the plots. Dung weights and calculated herbivore densities are recorded on data sheets. Frequency of monitoring is 6 monthly and ongoing.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: MINNAWARRA (SEG) MLR Long Term Biodiversity Survey

Long term monitoring of 8 bushland sites at Minnawarra (Heritage Agreement) which have been fenced from stock grazing. Project initiated by Scientific Expedition Group (SEG) in April 2001. Vegetation, mammals, birds, reptiles recorded, sites surveyed over 4 days twice a year (spring and autumn) and also visited by South Australian Museum (SAM). Animals are trapped using cage traps (2/site) Eliott traps (15/site) and pitfall traps (6/site).Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Pinkawillinie Vegetation Project

For the Land Systems mapping of the Gawler Ranges in 1987, three photopoint type sites were established in Pinkawillinie Conservation Park. The Land Systems mapping was an Inventory phase for Assessment of Pastoral stations within the region. These sites along with more recently established Biological Survey Sites (2001), potentially form a monitoring system for vegetation within the Park. Type Sites are not pegged sites, the locations maybe difficult to find from photography and grid coordinates taken from topographic small scale maps, there is limited quantitative information recorded.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Coorong and Lower Lakes mudflat survey (Invertebrates)

This project aims to research the ecology of mud flats to subsequently manage environmental flows to better manage mudflats. This information will be linked to the "Habitat Mapping Database Coorong and Lower Lakes Survey", and may be included on the spatial database. Data is collected bi-annually (survey began 2004) from 26 GPS located sites. A sediment sample is taken, with attributes measured including: - Invertebrate composition - sediment composition - total organic content - water chemistryProcedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Distribution and Sex Ratio of Antechinus flavipes in Fragmented Habitats

Movement of Antechinus flavipes through, and its use of, various fragments of native vegetation adjacent Deep Creek Conservation Park in 2000-2002. Examines the presence of Antechinus, breeding rates, movement and home range of lactating females among the fragments. Fragments include linear strips of vegetation along road side, patches in paddocks and areas of pine trees in vicinity of Range Road. Sites in Deep Creek Conservation Park constitute a control for comparison; these habitats not being fragmented like the adjoining farmland.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Bookmark Fire Monitoring

Based on the Conservation lands north of the river: Danggali Conservation Park, Pooginook Conservation Park, Cooltong Conservation Park, Chowilla Regional Reserve, Gluepot Reserve (Birds Australia), Calperum and Taylorville Stations (Environment Australia). The emphasis on this project is preserving the Mallee area, the effects of grazing on vegetation and the vegetation recovery after fire. Particularily in regards to threatened plant species and how to tailor a burn to suit their needs. With the possibility of breaking blocks up with fire breaks to avoid fires burning the areas with threatened species.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Fire Break and Access Track Monitoring (Lower Fleuireu Peninsula)

Assess regrowth along firebreaks and access tracks to determine the maintenance required and the frequency of treatment for their continued and effective use. Also assessing the impact of treatment on native vegetation immediately adjoining fire tracks. Treatment included the slashing and spraying of vegetation. Project prompted by concerns that fire track establishment and maintenance is detrimental to Park. Initial conclusions were that treatments did not affect adjoining vegetation. Monitoring ceased when it was determined that vegetation near the tracks showed no impact.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Level 3 joint atmosphere product (Curtin U) - MODIS

The Level 3 Atmospheric product provides statistical information on satellite derived aerosol retrievals, water vapour retrievals, cloud properties and atmosphere profiles. Each monthly file contains approximately 800 data sets while each daily file contains approximately 600 data sets. The data sets include histograms, mean, standard deviation, minimum and maximum values of each parameter as well as comparative histograms between parameters. A complete list of the data sets available for the monthly product and daily product are listed below

These products are generated from the Moderate Resolution Imaging Spectroradiometer (MODIS) instrument aboard the EOS satellites; Terra (morning descending orbit) and Aqua (afternoon ascending orbit).

Data sourced from the Level 1 and Atmosphere Archive and Distribution System (LAADS Web).These data should be cited as made available by through TERN/AusCover and accessed on

Biological Database of South Australia: Fire Response at Pinkawillinie Conservation Park (Don Driscoll)

Mallee vegetation covered 383,000 square kilometres of Australia but 35% of that has been cleared (Federal Dpt Environment and Heritage, http://audit.ea.gov.au/anra/vegetation). Remnant mallee occurs as isolated fragments throughout Australia's wheat and sheep producing lands, and harbours important biodiversity. However, altered fire regimes are potentially a serious threat to the survival of species in isolated mallee remnants. Single large fires could burn out entire remnants, eliminating fire sensitive species, or complete fire suppression could eliminate early successional species. Because remnants are isolated, there would be no opportunity for recolonisation resulting in widespread species declines. Our broad aim is to develop solutions to the problems posed by altered fire regimes in remnant vegetation. We plan to conduct a large-scale replicated experiment examining the response of plant and animal species to fire and fire frequency, and to examine the role of refuges in the recovery of populations after fire. The mechanism of recolonisation after fire is poorly understood, but knowledge of the mechanism is critical for the development of fire regimes that will conserve biodiversity in production landscapes. We will focus on remnant mallee ecosystems on the Eyre Peninsula, South Australia. Observations were conducted at Hincks, Hambridge, Munyaroo, Heggaton and Pinkawillinie Conservation Park from 2004-2006.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Biological Survey of South Australia: Buckland Park Environs

Surveyed in August/September 2006, 7 sites within 2 parcels of land in order to increase the knowledge of vegetation at Buckland Park (via entry to the Biological Survey of SA) and to contribute to the refinement of vegetation community mapping in the area. A complete list of plant species per 30m x 30m quadrat was obtained using braun/Blanquet cover abundance scores.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Biological Survey of South Australia: Pureba

A study surveying the Pureba Conservation Park and Nunnyah Conservation Reserve to obtain baseline data for PIRSA Mines & Energy 'Pureba/Nunnyah Rehabilitation Project', which is investigating regeneration of native vegetation on mineral exploration tracks; and to improve vegetation sample coverage in the area, complimenting the existing Yellabina Survey vegetation quadrats.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Biological Survey of South Australia: Para Wirra Recreation Park (NPWS 1981)

The Para Wirra Recreation Park was surveyed in 1978 to sample the vegetation of the range of vegetation associations systematically, using a series of grids and to map the major vegetation associations using aerial photography. The survey also sampled vertebrate fauna at a series of sites within each vegetation association in a systematic and repeatable way.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Biological Survey of South Australia: Innes National Park

This biological survey involved the collation of existing information on the biology of Innes National Park (Yorke Peninsula, South Australia) together with systematic sampling during the period of the survey. Biological Database of South Australia: Fauna Population Study: Coorong and Lakes Water Birds

This project aims to monitor migratory wader populations in the Coorong National Park, and subsequently help influence management systems and other strategies for the area, including water flow. The data will be analysed, and a report produced annually, the first being ready by the start of the financial year 2005. There will also be some comparison with other data sets.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Conservation Significance Analysis and Mapping in Council Areas: Remnant Native Grasslands in the Mt Lofty Ranges

Survey conducted (1998-2001) to locate a range of grassland habitats in the Southern Mount Lofty Ranges, to record the main plant species, qualitatively describe the plant community and landscape and condition; and to describe its current conservation status and management requirements. Prepared for the Native Grass Resource Group. Methodology consisted of a general walk through the remnant native grasslands, with a list of the most prominent species recorded.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Biological Survey of South Australia: Marqualpie

The Marqualpie Land System, in the Innamincka Regional Reserve, was surveyed between 1989 and 1992. Biological Database of South Australia: Thidna (York Peninsula) saline Vegetation Survey

This survey assessed the vegetation surrounding & within the main saline plain at Thidna Reserve. It aimed to obtain a picture of the ecological health of remnant native vegetation and the current impacts upon. Sites were selected to provide a holistic representation of the reserve, especially surrounding the saline plain. Each quadrat was chosen to represent a different plant association.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: MISC. RECORDS - JANE COOPER BIRD DATA

Project set up to accomodate Bird records from Jane Cooper. These records come from a variety of personal projects that Jane has carried out since about 1975. Biological Database of South Australia: Brush-Cutting Monitoring

This study involved three regions within South Australia - Kangaroo Island, Murray Mallee and Eyre Peninsula. Within these regions the study boundaries were based on the distribution of brush (Melaleuca uncinata). Aims of this survey were to: measure density of Melaleuca uncinata (broombush) communities, identify species associated with Melaleuca uncinata, estimate rate of regrowth of harvested Melaleuca uncinata, estimate yield of Melaleuca uncinata communities for brush fences and to map extent of Melaleuca uncinata communities in the North Eastern Eyre Peninsula.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Biological Survey of South Australia: Shirrocoe Management Plan Survey

Shirrocoe management plan survey contains flora data from Biological survey sites which were completed in May 2008. The survey also collected baseline data on fauna species present. Ecosystem health monitoring program developed in response to construction of the Tilley Swamp Drain. Biological Database of South Australia: Biological Survey of South Australia: Beetaloo Valley (Nature Conservation Society)

The Beetaloo Valley Catchment area was surveyed to identify and map important habitats and determine their biodiversity needs. In collaboration with relevant landowners, this information will be used to develop on ground management actions. Looking at catchment wide problems, feral animals as well as the maintenance of small areas of habitat in good condition. Landowners also will be encouraged to enter management agreements for areas of high biodiversity values.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Survey conducted between 1999 to 2000 to systematically sample the vertebrate fauna and all of the main vegetation types in the Upper South East area using the standard Biological Survey of South Australia methodology. The information gained from this exercise will be used to help plan the location of proposed drains in the area to minimise any potential impacts.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem / Biological Database of South Australia: Biological Survey of South Australia: Canunda Conservation Reserve

The objectives of this survey were to establish sites for long-term monitoring of vegetation in selected parts of Canunda Conservation Reserve (Lake Frome) and to identify the threats and long tem native vegetation management requirements for this wetland. The survey sites were chosen to include sites that have been recently grazed by cattle and sites which have not been grazed for 7-10 years. To determine the impact of grazing on the wetland plant communities as well as the impact or an altered drainage regime. Ten permanent photopoints were set up to monitor changes in plant community distribution and composition over time.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Vegetation Monitoring at Fairview, Deep and Tilley Swamp Drains

This project aims to monitor the impacts on native vegetation of the installation of the new Fairview, Deep and Tilley Swamp drains. The first sampling was done in 2000 and annual sampling was conducted until 2003, with the possibility of further sampling in five and ten years. Initial monitoring has shown that there is some localised detrimental effects at Hansen, otherwise no dramatic effects are evident - see reports for further details. Annual surveys are conducted using two techniques: (1) Transects of 500m length. Every ten metres, the density and health of Melaleuca halmaturorum and Melaleuca brevifolia was recorded for a 2 metre width each side of the transect. (2) Step point data - a set area is stepped out and whatever is stepped on is recorded - this technique records all species.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Kat Fish Reach project (Katarapko Tree Health)

The aim of this survey was to assess the health of trees as at 2007 within the study area and map accordingly.The study area consisted of the Murray River National Park that encompasses Katarapko Island to the extent of the 1956 flood level. The tree health assessments methodology was developed in conjunction with CSIRO to determine the health status of dominant trees, where health was assessed on a scale of 0-5 and each tree was assessed by the proportion of original canopy still present. 10 trees were sampled in each transect.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Rare and Threatened Species Protection Strategies: Stick-Nest Rat Release and Monitoring program on St. Peters Island

Captive bred Stick-Nest rats were reintroduced at 3 sites on St Peters Island on 4 occasions during the years 1993 - 1994. Intensive monitoring was undertaken during 1993 - 1995, then annually till 1998. 101 animals were monitored for distribution, survival and breeding status using radio transmitters, trapping and tracking observations. Trapping was conducted with Elliotts and pitfalls and tracks recorded along 200 metre transects set up at 11 track monitoring stations located along the road network. Radio-tracking was conducted during initial monitoring to determine home ranges size and overlap which enabled a suitable sized trapping grid to be designed and established. Owl pellets were also collected and examined for Stick-Nest rat remains.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Rare and Threatened Species Protection Strategies: Swamp Antechinus Distribution (Bachmann 1999-2001)

The objectives of this project were as follows: -To improve understanding of the distribution, abundance, habitat use and status of the mainland Swamp Antechinus in the South East of South Australia; -To define in particular, the extent of occurrence of the Swamp Antechinus within remnant Silky Tea-tree wet heath in near coastal areas between Kingston and the Victorian border; -To collect tissue samples that will form the basis of a future genetic study of South Australian populations of the Swamp Antechinus. - to confirm and where possible refine details for any records up until 2001 (some of these records come from other projects and sources.)Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Fauna Population Study: Penguin Population Monitoring on Granite and West Islands

Examine effects of tourism development on penguin colony of Granite Island by measuring trends in penguin populations. Trends in the Granite Island colony are compared with those of West Island, which is a control site, being less exposed to tourists. Initially undertaken to compare population numbers on Granite and West Islands. Measure breeding success by mapping occupied burrows, noting their repeated habitation and the presence of chicks. Survey north side and south of Granite Island as the impact site, and the north and south sides of West Island as the control site. West Island is control for tourist impacted area of Granite Island. Burrow occupation checked yearly, but population census done every six months.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Pastoral Management: Strzelecki Grazing Assessment

Tinga Tingana Pastoral Lease was assessed in July 2000 under the Pastoral Act. Grazing Photopoints were installed off major waterholes and evaluation of condition made. The lease is to be surrendered, the land merged with Strzelecki Regional Reserve and new grazing lease issued (under NP&WS Act) over portion of the lands. Existing photopoints and paddock descriptions will form the basis of future evaluation of grazing impacts within the Park. Biological Database of South Australia: Rare and Threatened Species Protection Strategies: Nest Box Survey of Feathertail Gliders

The aim of the survey was to determine the status and distribution of the Feathertail Glider Acrobates pygmaeus. Twenty sites were surveyed in the lower South East using nestboxes, trapping and hairtubes. Fourteen sites were surveyed close to the Murray River near Renmark to determine the presence of the Gliders. Hairtubes did not pick up the presence of the Feathertail Glider. Two individual Feathertail Gliders were captured in traps from a single remnant in the South East, and two were recorded from one nest box in the Riverland. The extent of the survey included 1 300 trap nights and 326 nestboxes in 1999/2000.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Pastoral Management: Kangaroo Aerial Survey

The Kangaroo aerial survey project contains approximately 20 years (Starting from 1978) of data that has been collected by various people. Whilst counting Western Grey and Red Kangaroo numbers, counts for Emu's and camels were also collected and any other significant sightings. The flight path varies from year to year so anyone trying to interpret population numbers or compare years needs to contact the custodians about exact methodology. The Kangaroo count data is used to Prepare Management Plans to set annual harvest quotas and sustainably manage kangaroo populations on pastoral properties.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Pastoral Management: Chowilla Vegetation Exclosures Monitoring Study (Coombool Paddock)

Herbivore exclosures were set up on Chowilla Pastoral Lease in 1986 to determine the effects of grazing and grazing suppression on populations of Atriplex stipitata. This species dominates a commonly found land system and is seldom grazed by stock unless other palatable species have been removed through unsustainable grazing . Two fenced treatments (exclude all herbivores and a Rabbit Entry only) and a control were spatially mapped for mature and seedling shrubs. Step-point plant cover measurements were also taken within the treatments along with photographs and shrub dimension data. Chowilla lease has been reverted to regional reserve status. Studies were jointly organised between the Dept. of Lands Outback Region & Salisbury College of Advanced Education.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Vegetation and Water Quality Demonstration Sites at Brown Hill Creek

Demonstration site was established in 1999, along Brown Hill Creek as part of the OurPatch program of the Patawolonga Catchment Board. Weeds were cleared and native regrowth encouraged to demonstrate link between natural riparian systems and water quality. Monitoring system established belatedly as part of the Education focus. In 2002 an additional area cleared of willows (Manure Pits Site) and monitoring system devised at the time. Plant regrowth and the restoration of riparian ecosystems are the principal monitoring foci. Photopoints are also considered an additional means of showing the community the benefits of restoring riparian ecosystems.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Rare and Threatened Species Protection Strategies: Yellow-Tailed Black-Cockatoo Baseline Biological Surveys on Private Land

The efforts of the community and certain landholders have been instrumental to the success of the Eyre Peninsula Yellow-tailed Black-Cockatoo (EPYTBC) project thus far. One of the ongoing objectives of the project is to continue fostering community awareness and support for the EPYTBC, which, through the principles of being a flagship species, can in turn protect and highlight the status of other threatened species on Eyre Peninsula. The EPYTBC Recovery Team feel it is important to be reciprocal in conservation efforts with landholders and feel one way of continuing this awareness and mutual benefit of working together is to offer key landholders the opportunity of a basic flora and fauna survey conducted on their property's remnant vegetation.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Rare and Threatened Species Protection Strategies: Threatened Plant Monitoring at Mokota Conservation Park

This program was conducted in Oct 1999 and monitored the nationally threatened plant species Cullen parvum and Dodanaea procumbens in Mokota Conservation Park. The projects aims were to: - Determine if the removal of stock grazing results in increased recruitment and survival of Cullen parvum and Dodanaea procumbens plants. - Determine if the removal of stock grazing results in increased weed invasion in the vicinity of Cullen parvum and Dodanaea procumbens populations in the park. - Determine if the removal of stock grazing results in increased competition from other native species. - Determine if park management - in particular weed, feral animal, and fire management - is adequate and appropriate for the management of these species.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Riparian Zone Management in Sturt Gorge

Restoration of native plant communities along 3 km of riparian zone of Sturt River. Removal of elm, ash, olive and boxthorn to promote regeneration of native plants under more natural light regimes. Follow-up spraying to reduce weed competition with emerging native plants. Emphasis on 10 m each side of the river. Monitoring is desirable to determine kill rate and level of natural regeneration, so as to decide whether to let regrowth occur naturally or plant tubestock . Some eyeball evaluations of responses so far have been made. Simple photopoint system intended for monitoring. 3 km of Sturt River length treated, but photopoints may only cover sections of creek.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Fire Vegetation Monitoring in Coorong NP (Wreck Crossing & Potters Land)

Fires occurred at 2 localities within the Coorong National Park during November and December 1990, photopoint monitoring sites were established during April 1991 to assess the response mechanisms of plants species recorded in two height structures. The fire at Potters Landing consumed most of the park and therefore the monitoring sites act as their own controls. Another small fire occurred at Wreck Point where two monitoring sites including a control were established. Quadrats and sub quadrats were measured to determine plant densities, aerial cover and regenerative mechanisms of individual species. Species list including alien species were also collected. A proposal to conduct a direct seeding trial of the Long Point fire area has been put up by Woods & Forest which will include fencing off the Potters Scrub to control rabbits as an aid to rehabilitation.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Rare and Threatened Species Protection Strategies: Spiny Daisy ( Acanthocladium dockeri) Project

This species was presumed extinct before it was re-discovered in 1999 by Paul Slattery, a farmer from Laura and identified by the State Herbarium. It was found 200 km from where it was previously thought to occur. Over the next few years 3 additional populations were found on the roadsides in the Mid North. All plants at each site were found to be genetically identical. Weed control at these sites has been carried out since re-discovery. A monitoring program for the Spiny Daisy is carried out annually. This dataset decribes the known location and extent of this threatened plant.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Glossy Black Cockatoo Recovery Program Kangaroo Island. Program outcomes 2005-06 The South Australian Glossy Black Cockatoo Recovery Plan implemented with: - Breeding and survivorship of the population monitored through nest observation and banding and observation of individual birds. - Population dynamics monitored through an annual population census. - Nest sites protected from predators and competitors. - Volunteer program developed to equip and coordinate volunteers with the skills necessary to support the recovery process. - General media, scientific, school and community presentations and print articles developed to facilitate publis awareness and community ownership of the Recovery Program. - Feeding and nesting habitat protected, restored and expanded.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Ad-hoc opportunistic flora and fauna species records: BUPRESTIDAE OF SOUTH AUSTRALIA

The Buprestidae survey was conducted in 2006, across the entire state of South Australia (with some records from interstate also.) It aimed to compile detailed voucher and sight records of Buprestidae (Jewel Beetle) species to support various projects relating to this group, including: investigation of phylogenetic relationships using DNA sequencing, DNA barcoding for species identification (adult and larval phases), analysis of plant host - insect relationships, determination of conservation status and the implications for 'No species loss', determing the impacts of habitat clearance and degradation, and investigations of potential impacts of climate change on susceptible species. At each site the dominant plants for each site were to be recorded.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Bool Lagoon Fire Response Monitoring

This Bool Lagoon project includes pre and post-burn monitoring. Data is collected on different plant responses to fire. There are three quadrats per site which are surveyed. Attributes include species, cover and abundance. Photopoints were used. A prescribed burn was done in the area in Spring 2003. Since then there have been two site visits (surveys). There has been rapid regeneration since the burn in Spring 2003, with abundance levels similar to pre-burn figures. The resulting information will contribute to Management Plans and assist in planning fire regimes.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Monitoring Dredged Sand Deposits - Katarapko Game Reserve

In 1979 and 1982 EWS dredged sand from the main channel of the River Murray and a percentage deposited at 4 sites within the Katarapko Game Reserve. A program was established to monitor the effects of dredged sand on the river bank flora and how flooding influences the depth and distribution of sand. 4 sites have been located off Rilli and Media Islands with 3 X 4 metre quadrats placed to measure rooted and overhanging plants, species and percentage cover on an annual basis. Dredged sand depths are measured at 2 sites immediately following a flood event and all sites are photographed. Pre/post dredge data and photos (print/slide) collected by park rangers.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Fauna Population Study: Feral and Native Fauna Monitoring in Witjira NP and Simpson Desert CP

During June 2001 aerial transects of the Witjira National Park and Simpson Desert Conservation Park were flown to determine feral animal abundance/distribution and to establish a methodology and logistical requirements for future surveys contributing toward management of feral herbivores within the reserved areas. Various eradication programs have been concentrated within the Simpson Desert region by NPWSA and through local soil boards but populations have never been verified to determine success rates. As an adjunct to the survey, opportunistic sightings of native fauna were also recorded. Transects were flown over both parks in November 2001 using recognised counting procedures with experienced operators. Culling operations of feral herbivores were subsequently conducted both within the reserved areas and adjacent pastoral leases.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Grazing monitoring for Mud Islands

This project aims to determine a sustainable grazing regime for the Mud Island Game Reserve, via monitoring of the native vegetation in response to differing stock numbers. The landholders are closely worked with, and stock regimes implemented that aim to benefit the landholder and the conservation of the area. Survey began in 2004 and is still going. Data is collected via a point based system and a subjective visual assessment of the native vegetation. The number of stock that has been on the property is recorded, and the resulting condition of the ground and the native vegetation. The number of stock will then be adjusted, and the effects of a different number of stock assessed seasonally, (four times a year). Attributes recorded include: - dominant plant species list; - condition of vegetation using standard assessment criteria; - changes in distribution and abundanceProcedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Conservation Significance Analysis and Mapping in Council Areas: Directory of Important Wetlands (Report)

Hardcopy report of wetlands throughout Australia. South Australian section has 69 wetlands. Wetlands were researched from existing references and data sources (ie. no new field work). Lists wetlands of national importance, according to criteria specified in the report. Notable plant species only for each wetland are listed, that is, if they are nationally or State threatened. Information on the composition of any plant spcies or communities for which the wetland is particularly important is also included. Notable fauna are listed: that is natioanally or State threatened fauna. Also includes information on composition of important fauna that may inhabit the wetland permanently or seasonally, including migratory species. An indication of population sizes, breeding colonies, migration stopover etc is also given where available.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Plant Fire Response Monitoring (Statewide South Australia)

This is a state wide project, covering all tenures but focussed on reserves. It aims to determine different plant responses to disturbance, predominantly fire, but not exclusively. This information will then be used to develop appropriate fire regimes. Data is collected in relation to both natural fires and prescribed burns. For prescribed burns the plants are often tagged prior to the burn to allow identification following the fire. Alternatively areas with known fire histories are studied, and plant characteristics and regrowth noted. Note that data collection is opportunistic for wildfires and prescribed burns, however there is a methodology followed, outlined in a hand book that includes field attributes. Data collected includes: - regeneration of plants. - response and regeneration of soil seed blown in. - time taken to develop mature seed. - life expectancy. - voucher specimens if necessary for identification.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. The licence lets others distribute, remix, tweak, and build upon the work, even commercially, as long as they credit the owner for the original creation.

Biological Database of South Australia: Natural Hazard Protection: Ngarkat CP fire monitoring

Monitoring in Ngarkat Conservation Park is conducted for each major vegetation type occuring within the burn area. If the burn area is greater than 1 ha then a number of monitoring sites within the burn are made. The vegetation is surveyed before the burn, immediately after, one year after and then every 3 years after that. The sampling includes setting up photopoints, doing a Ramble survey of plant species, and fixed quadrats and transects. Photopoints are at the same sites as the quadrat sites. Monoitoring will measure fuel hazard, environmental risks, vegetation floristics/ structure and key habitat factors. During the burn information is recorded on the weather, and post fire the survey is repeated. Each prescribed burn has a pre and post assessment and is entered in to the Fire database. The frequency of the burn depends on weather, previous year and other factors. The rates of regeneration can be monitored and the response of biota to fire and drought.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Monitoring Program- Katarapko Island Evaporation Basin - Katarapko Game Reserve

E&WS constructed an evaporation basin in Yabby Creek (Katarapko Game Reserve Island) and adjacent lagoons to contain fruit juice waste. The monitoring program was devised after an Environmental Impact Statement showed there had been devastating impacts to the original environment. Six photopoints have been set up to seasonally monitor semi aquatic vegetation, lignum shrubs and river red gum regeneration with monthly bird surveys to ascertain breeding populations, nesting sites etc. and cover of individual species. Environmental Impact Statement produced monitoring data and photos collected in 1982 and 1989.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Native Vegetation Assessment Program: Murraylands Biodiversity Hotspots Project

The aim of this project is to protect remnant vegetation on private land to be put under a Heritage Agreement. Staff member from DEH is liasing with land owners who wish to formally protect their remnant vegetation under a Heritage Agreement. He has discussed this with 5 land owners to date (6/4/2005) and 4 of those have put applications to the Native Vegetation Group for a Heritage Agreement. He has been approaching land owners with large blocks of native vegetation, in the future he will also include smaller blocks of land with significant vegetation. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Onkaparinga Wetland Restoration and Revegetation

Since 1992, wetlands have been constructed and degraded areas revegetated in the estuary, swamp and adjoining parts of Onkaparinga Estuary. Native flora was planted in five wetlands, each receiving stormwater from adjoining urban subdivisions. Non-riparian lands, which were previously grazed, were extensively revegetated from 1998 onwards. In order to protect regrowing vegetation, a goat eradication program is underway. Establishing a monitoring program would reveal which plant species have survived, identifying likely requirements for successful regeneration of various native species. Details of the actual planting specifications (plant species, locations, times etc) are available. Revegetation, species and areas to replant, closely follow original specifications. Goat control involves shooting over three days, twice a year, and recording the numbers shot.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Biological Database of South Australia: Rare and Threatened Species Protection Strategies: Wandillo NFR Post-fire Southern Brown Bandicoot Digging Abundance Monitoring

This project aims to establish if Southern Brown Bandicoots survived after the February 2000 fire in Wandillo Fire Reserve. David Paull's walking transect methodology (diggings) is used to assess bandicoot population abundance. This involves walking an established loop of 100-150 metres and counting the diggings and allocating an age class (fresh, recent, old) to the digging. Approximately 12 sites (transects) were assessed in areas that were known to be good historic bandicoot habitats. The first survey was conducted in Mid-2000 and it is hoped that the area can be revisited every 6-12 months, at any time of year.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. BHP Billiton requires a fauna survey and potential impact study assessment of the proposed infrastructure corridor between Whyalla and Olympic Dam. Biological Database of South Australia: Monitoring - Vegetation/Ecosystem: Experimental Vegetation Management at Mokota Conservation Park

The experimental trial was established to assess the need for biomass reduction to conserve the temperate native grassland at Mokota Conservation Park. The managment aims to maintain the plant species diversity of the grassland and whether the reduction of plant litter and living plant biomass would achieve this goal. The 9 plots of 2.9 hetares were established in 2002 in native grassland in the north west section of the park. The biomass was reduced by 1.Burning in Autumn 2. Sheep grazing twice in winter 3. control plots and a 50 x 50 m kangaroo exclosure was established in each fire plot. The presence or absence of every plant species was recorded for 50 square quadrats of 30 cm x 30 cm located along each set of transects. The frequency of plant species in 2002 and 2003 are compared.Procedures for accessing data within the Biological Database of South Australia are described at http://www.environment.sa.gov.au/Knowledge_Bank/Information_data/Biological_databases_of_South_Australia .This data is subject to conditions described in the Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 Unported (CC BY 3.0) licence. Samford Flux CO2 tower

Data from the Samford Valley flux station at the Samford Ecological Reserach Facility.
The data is part OzFlux, a national ecosystem research network consisting of 10 flux stations at present with a further 6 planned for installation in 2011.
The OzFlux network will provide the Australian and global ecosystem modelling communities with nationally consistent observations of energy, carbon and water exchange between the atmosphere and key Australian ecosystems.
OzFlux is part of an international network (FluxNet) of over 500 flux stations that is designed to provide continuous, long-term micrometeorological measurements to monitor the state of ecosystems globally.
Data from the Samford Flux tower is available at: http://ozflux.its.monash.edu.au/ecosystem/pub/viewColDetails.jspx?collection.id=200&collection.owner.id=155&viewType=anonymous
